padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Linguasphere_Observatory" title="Linguasphere Observatory">Linguasphere</a></th>\n<td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code>59-AAF-qa to -qf</code></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hindustani_map.png" class="image"><img alt="Hindustani map.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Hindustani_map.png/220px-Hindustani_map.png" width="220" height="204" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Hindustani_map.png/330px-Hindustani_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Hindustani_map.png/440px-Hindustani_map.png 2x" data-file-width="877" data-file-height="814" /></a>\n<div style="text-align:left;">Areas (red) where Hindustani (Khariboli/Kauravi) is the native language</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" class="noprint selfref" style="text-align:center;background-color:#ddddff;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Replacement_character" class="mw-redirect" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/40px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png" width="40" height="37" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/60px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/80px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="103" data-file-height="94" /></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><i><b><a href="https://hi.wikipedia.org/wiki/" class="extiw" title="hi:">Hindi edition</a></b></i> of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>, the free encyclopedia</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/40px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png" width="40" height="37" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/60px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/80px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="103" data-file-height="94" /></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><i><b><a href="https://ur.wikipedia.org/wiki/" class="extiw" title="ur:">Urdu edition</a></b></i> of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>, the free encyclopedia</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hindustani</b> (Hindustani: <span lang="hin" xml:lang="hin"><span class="Unicode">\xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa4\xbf\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa5\x81\xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xa4\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa5\x80</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[a]</a></sup> <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';">\xdb\x81\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xdb\x8c</span>\xe2\x80\x8e<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[b]</a></sup> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA/Hindi and Urdu">[\xcb\x8c\xc9\xa6\xc9\xaand\xcc\xaa\xca\x8as\xcb\x88t\xcc\xaaa\xcb\x90ni\xcb\x90]</a></span></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&#160;</small>\'"of <a href="/wiki/Hindustan" title="Hindustan">Hindustan</a>"\'<sup id="cite_ref-NCSU-Hindustani_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCSU-Hindustani-9">[7]</a></sup>), historically also known as <b>Hindavi</b>, <b>Dehlavi</b> and <b>Rekhta</b>, is the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-siddiqi1994_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siddiqi1994-10">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pulsipher2005_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pulsipher2005-11">[9]</a></sup> It is an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan language</a>, deriving its base primarily from the <a href="/wiki/Khariboli_dialect" title="Khariboli dialect">Khariboli dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>. The language incorporates a large amount of vocabulary from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geomag1935jsh_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geomag1935jsh-12">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jrsa1948hae_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jrsa1948hae-13">[11]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Pluricentric_language" title="Pluricentric language">pluricentric language</a>, with two official forms, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Modern Standard Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Modern Standard Urdu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nunley1999_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nunley1999-14">[12]</a></sup> which are its <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standardised</a> <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">registers</a>, and which may be called <b>Hindustani</b> or <b>Hindi-Urdu</b> when taken together.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> The colloquial registers are mostly indistinguishable, and even though the official standards are nearly identical in grammar, they differ in literary conventions and in academic and technical vocabulary, with Urdu adopting stronger Persian and Arabic influences, and Hindi relying more heavily on Sanskrit.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> Before the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of the British Indian Empire</a>, the terms <i>Hindustani, Urdu,</i> and <i>Hindi</i> were synonymous; all covered what would be mostly called Urdu and Hindi today.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-18">[16]</a></sup> The term <i>Hindustani</i> is still used for the colloquial language and the <i>lingua franca</i> of North India and Pakistan, for example for the language of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> films, as well as for several quite different <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Hindi" class="mw-redirect" title="Varieties of Hindi">varieties of Hindi</a> spoken outside the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Subcontinent">Indian Subcontinent</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Fiji_Hindi" title="Fiji Hindi">Fiji Hindi</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Caribbean Hindustani</a> of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, and the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. Hindustani is also spoken by a small number of people in <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Bazaar_Hindustani"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bazaar Hindustani</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Official_status"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Official status</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Hindustani_outside_South_Asia"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Hindustani outside South Asia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Phonology"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Phonology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Grammar"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Grammar</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Vocabulary"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Vocabulary</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Writing_system"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Writing system</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Sample_text"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Sample text</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Formal_Hindi"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Formal Hindi</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Formal_Urdu"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Formal Urdu</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Hindustani_and_Bollywood"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Hindustani and Bollywood</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Urdu_films_and_Lollywood"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Urdu films and Lollywood</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hindustani" title="History of Hindustani">History of Hindustani</a></div>\n<p>Early forms of present-day Hindustani developed from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Middle Indo-Aryan languages">Middle Indo-Aryan</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Apabhramsha" class="mw-redirect" title="Apabhramsha">apabhramsha</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernaculars</a> of present-day <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a> in the 7th\xe2\x80\x9313th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-brown2008_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown2008-19">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amir_Khusro" class="mw-redirect" title="Amir Khusro">Amir Khusro</a>, who lived in the 13th century CE during the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> period in North India, used these forms (which was the <i>lingua franca</i> of the period) in his writings and referred to it as <i>Hindavi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-brown2008_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown2008-19">[17]</a></sup> The Delhi Sultanate, which comprised several <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Afghanistan" title="Demographics of Afghanistan">Afghan</a> dynasties that ruled from Delhi,<sup id="cite_ref-Gat_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gat-20">[18]</a></sup> was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> in 1526.</p>\n<p>Although the Mughals were of <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timurid</a> (<i>Gurk\xc4\x81n\xc4\xab</i>) <a href="/wiki/Turko-Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Turko-Mongol">Turko-Mongol</a> descent,<sup id="cite_ref-Thackston_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thackston-21">[19]</a></sup> they were <a href="/wiki/Persianization" title="Persianization">Persianised</a>, and Persian had gradually become the state language of the Mughal empire after <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EI_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Columbia_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> a continuation since the introduction of Persian by <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Asian">Central Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> rulers in the Indian Subcontinent,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> and the patronisation of it by the earlier Turko-Afghan Delhi Sultanate. The basis in general for the introduction of Persian language into the subcontinent was set, from its earliest days, by various Persianised Central Asian Turkic and Afghan dynasties.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the 18th century, towards the end of the Mughal period, with the fragmentation of the empire and the elite system, a variant of <a href="/wiki/Khariboli" class="mw-redirect" title="Khariboli">Khariboli</a>, one of the successors of apabhramsha vernaculars at <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, and nearby cities, came to gradually replace Persian as the <i>lingua franca</i> among the educated elite <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper class</a> particularly in northern India, though Persian still retained much of its pre-eminence for a short period. The term <i>Hindustani</i> (literally "of <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan" title="Hindustan">Hindustan</a></i>") was the name given to that variant of Khariboli.</p>\n<p>For socio-political reasons, though essentially the variant of <a href="/wiki/Khariboli" class="mw-redirect" title="Khariboli">Khariboli</a> with Persian vocabulary, the emerging <a href="/wiki/Prestige_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestige dialect">prestige dialect</a> became also known as <i>Urdu</i> (properly <i>zab\xc4\x81n-e Urdu-e mo\'alla</i> "language of the court" or <i>zab\xc4\x81n-e Urdu</i> <span lang="fa" dir="rtl" xml:lang="fa">\xd8\xb2\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88</span>\xe2\x80\x8e, \xe0\xa4\x9c\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa4\xac\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xa8-\xe0\xa4\x8f \xe0\xa4\x89\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa5\x82, "language of the camp" in Persian, derived from <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> <i>Ord\xc5\xab</i> "camp", cognate with English <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/horde" class="extiw" title="wikt:Special:Search/horde">horde</a></i>; due to its origin as the common speech of the Mughal army). The more highly Persianised version later established as a language of the court was called <i><a href="/wiki/Rekhta" title="Rekhta">Rekhta</a></i>, or "mixed".</p>\n<p>As an emerging common dialect, Hindustani absorbed large numbers of Persian, Arabic, and Turkic words, and as Mughal conquests grew it spread as a <i>lingua franca</i> across much of northern India. Written in the <a href="/wiki/Perso-Arabic_Script" class="mw-redirect" title="Perso-Arabic Script">Perso-Arabic Script</a> or <a href="/wiki/Devanagari_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Devanagari script">Devanagari script</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mcgregor_912_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgregor_912-28">[26]</a></sup> it remained the primary <i>lingua franca</i> of northern India for the next four centuries (although it varied significantly in vocabulary depending on the local language) and achieved the status of a literary language, alongside Persian, in Muslim courts. Its development was centred on the poets of the Mughal courts of cities in <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> such as Delhi, <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/John_Fletcher_Hurst" title="John Fletcher Hurst">John Fletcher Hurst</a> in his book published in 1891 mentioned that the Hindustani or Camp language or Language of the Camps of <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Moughal</a> courts at <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> was not regarded by philologists as distinct language but only as a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> with admixture of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>. He continued: "But it has all the magnitude and importance of separate language. It is linguistic result of Muslim rule of eleventh &amp; twelfth centuries and is spoken (except in rural <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> ) by many <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a> and by <a href="/wiki/Musalman" class="mw-redirect" title="Musalman">Musalman</a> population in all parts of India". Next to English it was the official language of <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="British Indian Empire">British Indian Empire</a>, was commonly written in Arabic or Persian characters, and was spoken by approximately 100,000,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>When the British colonised the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> from the late 18th through to the late 19th century, they used the words \'Hindustani\', \'Hindi\' and \'Urdu\' interchangeably. They developed it as the language of administration of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.co.uk_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.co.uk-30">[28]</a></sup> further preparing it to be the official language of modern India and Pakistan. However, with independence, use of the word \'Hindustani\' declined, being largely replaced by \'Hindi\' and \'Urdu\', or \'Hindi-Urdu\' when either of those was too specific. More recently, the word \'Hindustani\' has been used for the colloquial language of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> films, which are popular in both India and Pakistan and which cannot be unambiguously identified as either Hindi or Urdu.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Registers">Registers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Registers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hindi%E2%80%93Urdu_controversy" title="Hindi\xe2\x80\x93Urdu controversy">Hindi\xe2\x80\x93Urdu controversy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">Register (sociolinguistics)</a></div>\n<p>Although, at the spoken level, Hindi and Urdu are considered <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">registers</a> of a single language, they differ vastly in literary and formal <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">vocabulary</a>; where literary Hindi draws heavily on Sanskrit and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Prakrit" title="Prakrit">Prakrit</a>, literary Urdu draws heavily on Persian and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>. The grammar and base vocabulary (most pronouns, verbs, adpositions, etc.) of both Hindi and Urdu, however, are the same and derive from a Prakritic base, and both have a Persian/Arabic influence.</p>\n<p>The standardised registers Hindi and Urdu are collectively known as <i>Hindi-Urdu</i>. Hindustani is perhaps the <i>lingua franca</i> of the north and west of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, though it is understood fairly well in other regions also, especially in the urban areas. A common vernacular sharing characteristics with Sanskritised Hindi, regional Hindi and Urdu, Hindustani is more commonly used as a vernacular than highly Sanskritised Hindi or highly Arabicised/Persianised Urdu.</p>\n<p>This can be seen in the popular culture of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> or, more generally, the vernacular of North Indians and Pakistanis, which generally employs a lexicon common to both <i>Hindi</i> and <i>Urdu</i> speakers. Minor subtleties in region will also affect the \'brand\' of Hindustani, sometimes pushing the Hindustani closer to Urdu or to Hindi. One might reasonably assume that the Hindustani spoken in <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> (known for its usage of Urdu) and <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a> (a holy city for Hindus and thus using highly Sanskritised Hindi) is somewhat different.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Standard_Hindi">Modern Standard Hindi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Modern Standard Hindi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rigveda_MS2097.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rigveda_MS2097.jpg/160px-Rigveda_MS2097.jpg" width="160" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rigveda_MS2097.jpg/240px-Rigveda_MS2097.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rigveda_MS2097.jpg/320px-Rigveda_MS2097.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1161" data-file-height="1125" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rigveda_MS2097.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Rigveda" title="Rigveda">Rigveda</a> manuscript in Devanagari (early 19th century)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a></div>\n<p>Standard Hindi, one of the <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Official languages of India">official languages of India</a>, is based on the <a href="/wiki/Khariboli" class="mw-redirect" title="Khariboli">Khariboli</a> dialect of the Delhi region and differs from Urdu in that it is usually written in the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a> script of India and exhibits less Persian and Arabic influence than Urdu. Many scholars today employ a Sanskritised form of Hindi developed primarily in <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> holy city, which is based on the Eastern Hindi dialect of that region and thus a separate language from official Standard Hindi.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It has a literature of 500 years, with prose, poetry, religion &amp; philosophy, under the Bahmani Kings and later on Khutab Shahi Adil Shahi etc. It is a living language, still prevalent all over the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan Plateau</a>. Note that the term <i>Hindustani</i> has generally fallen out of common usage in modern India, except to refer to "Indian" as a nationality<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> and a style of Indian <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">classical music prevalent in northern India</a>. The term used to refer to it is <i>Hindi</i> or <i>Urdu</i>, depending on the religion of the speaker, and regardless of the mix of Persian or Sanskrit words used by the speaker. One could conceive of a wide spectrum of dialects and registers, with the highly Persianised Urdu at one end of the spectrum and a heavily Sanskrit-based dialect, spoken in the region around <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a>, at the other end of the spectrum. In common usage in India, the term <i>Hindi</i> includes all these dialects except those at the Urdu end of the spectrum. Thus, the different meanings of the word <i>Hindi</i> include, among others:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>standardised Hindi as taught in schools throughout India (except some states such as Tamil Nadu),</li>\n<li>formal or official Hindi advocated by <a href="/wiki/Purushottam_Das_Tandon" title="Purushottam Das Tandon">Purushottam Das Tandon</a> and as instituted by the post-independence Indian government, heavily influenced by Sanskrit,</li>\n<li>the vernacular dialects of Hindustani as spoken throughout India,</li>\n<li>the neutralised form of Hindustani used in popular television and films, or</li>\n<li>the more formal neutralised form of Hindustani used in broadcast and print news reports.</li>\n</ol>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Standard_Urdu">Modern Standard Urdu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern Standard Urdu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zaban_urdu_mualla.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Zaban_urdu_mualla.png/165px-Zaban_urdu_mualla.png" width="165" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Zaban_urdu_mualla.png 1.5x" data-file-width="225" data-file-height="184" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zaban_urdu_mualla.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe phrase <i>Zab\xc4\x81n-e Urdu-e Mo\'alla</i> written in <a href="/wiki/Nasta%27liq" class="mw-redirect" title="Nasta\'liq">Nasta\'liq</a> calligraphy</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> is the national language of Pakistan and an officially recognised regional language of India. Urdu is the official language of all Pakistani provinces and is taught in all schools as a compulsory subject up to the 12th grade. It is also an official language in the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Territory_of_Delhi" class="mw-redirect" title="National Capital Territory of Delhi">National Capital Territory of Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> that have significant Muslim populations.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bazaar_Hindustani">Bazaar Hindustani</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bazaar Hindustani">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindi_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi dialects">Hindi dialects</a></div>\n<p>In a specific sense, <i>Hindustani</i> may be used to refer to the dialects and varieties used in common speech, in contrast with the standardised Hindi and Urdu. This meaning is reflected in the use of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> Hindustani</i>, in other words, the "language of the street or the marketplace", as opposed to the perceived refinement of formal Hindi, Urdu, or even Sanskrit. Thus, the Webster\'s New World Dictionary defines the term Hindustani as <i>the principal dialect of Hindi/Urdu, used as a trade language throughout north India and Pakistan.</i></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Amir_Khusro" class="mw-redirect" title="Amir Khusro">Amir Khusro</a> ca. 1300 referred to this language of his writings as <i>Dahlavi</i> (\'of Delhi\') or <i>Hindavi</i> (\xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa4\xbf\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa4\xb5\xe0\xa5\x80, <span lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';">\xdb\x81\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xdb\x8c</span>\xe2\x80\x8e</span> \'of <a href="/wiki/Hindustan" title="Hindustan">Hindustan</a>\'). During this period, Hindustani was used by <a href="/wiki/Sufis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufis">Sufis</a> in promulgating their message across the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Amri-Hindavi_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amri-Hindavi-32">[30]</a></sup> After the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Mughals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mughals">Mughals</a> in the subcontinent, Hindustani acquired more Persian loanwords. <i><a href="/wiki/Rekhta" title="Rekhta">Rekhta</a></i> (\'mixture\') and <i>Hindi</i> (of \'Hindustan\')<sup id="cite_ref-mcgregor_912_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgregor_912-28">[26]</a></sup> became popular names for the same language until the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-faruqi_806_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faruqi_806-33">[31]</a></sup> The name <i>Urdu</i> appeared around 1780.<sup id="cite_ref-faruqi_806_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faruqi_806-33">[31]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, the term <i>Hindustani</i> was used by British officials.<sup id="cite_ref-faruqi_806_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faruqi_806-33">[31]</a></sup> In 1796, <a href="/wiki/John_Borthwick_Gilchrist" class="mw-redirect" title="John Borthwick Gilchrist">John Borthwick Gilchrist</a> published a "A Grammar of the Hindoostanee Language".<sup id="cite_ref-faruqi_806_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faruqi_806-33">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gilchrist_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilchrist-34">[32]</a></sup> Upon <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition</a>, India and Pakistan established national standards that they called <i>Hindi</i> and <i>Urdu,</i> respectively, and attempted to make distinct, with the result that <i>Hindustani</i> commonly, but mistakenly, came to be seen as a <i>mixture</i> of Hindi and Urdu.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/George_Abraham_Grierson" title="George Abraham Grierson">Grierson</a>, in his highly influential <i><a href="/wiki/Linguistic_Survey_of_India" title="Linguistic Survey of India">Linguistic Survey of India</a></i>, proposed that the names <i>Hindustani, Urdu,</i> and <i>Hindi</i> be separated in use for different varieties of the Hindustani language, rather than as the overlapping synonyms they frequently were:</p>\n<blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p>We may now define the three main varieties of Hind\xc5\x8dst\xc4\x81n\xc4\xab as follows:\xe2\x80\x94Hind\xc5\x8dst\xc4\x81n\xc4\xab is primarily the language of the Upper Gangetic Doab, and is also the <i>lingua franca</i> of India, capable of being written in both Persian and D\xc4\x93va-n\xc4\x81gar\xc4\xab characters, and without purism, avoiding alike the excessive use of either Persian or Sanskrit words when employed for literature. The name \'Urd\xc5\xab\' can then be confined to that special variety of Hind\xc5\x8dst\xc4\x81n\xc4\xab in which Persian words are of frequent occurrence, and which hence can only be written in the Persian character, and, similarly, \'Hind\xc4\xab\' can be confined to the form of Hind\xc5\x8dst\xc4\x81n\xc4\xab in which Sanskrit words abound, and which hence can only be written in the D\xc4\x93va-n\xc4\x81gar\xc4\xab character.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup></p>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hindi_literature" title="Hindi literature">Hindi literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_literature" title="Urdu literature">Urdu literature</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_status">Official status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Official status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_asia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/South_asia.jpg/210px-South_asia.jpg" width="210" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/South_asia.jpg/315px-South_asia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/South_asia.jpg/420px-South_asia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="533" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_asia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHindustani, in its standardised registers, is one of the official languages of both India (Hindi) and Pakistan (Urdu).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hindi, a major standardized <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">register</a> of Hindustani, is declared by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a> as the "official language (r\xc4\x81jabh\xc4\x81sh\xc4\x81) of the Union" (Art. 343(1)) (In this context, "Union" means the Federal Government and not the entire country \xe2\x80\x93 India has <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Official languages of India">23 official languages</a>). At the same time, however, the definitive text of Federal laws is officially the English text and proceedings in the higher appellate courts must be conducted in English. At the state level, Hindi is one of the official languages in <a href="/wiki/Languages_with_official_status_in_India#Languages_currently_used_In_Indian_states_and_union_territories" title="Languages with official status in India">9 of the 29</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_state_and_UT_capitals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Indian state and UT capitals">Indian states</a> and three Union Territories (namely <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chhattisgarh" title="Chhattisgarh">Chhattisgarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a> and UTs are <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chandigarh" title="Chandigarh">Chandigarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a>). In the remaining states Hindi is not an official language. In the state of Tamil Nadu studying Hindi is not compulsory in the state curriculum. However an option to take the same as second or third language does exist. In many other states, studying Hindi is usually compulsory in the school curriculum as a third language (the first two languages being the state\'s official language and English), though the intensiveness of Hindi in the curriculum varies.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Urdu, also a major standardized register of Hindustani, is also one of the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Schedule_to_the_Indian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth Schedule to the Indian Constitution">languages recognized by the Indian Constitution</a> and is an official language of the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>. Although the government school system in most other states emphasises <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Hindi" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Standard Hindi">Modern Standard Hindi</a>, at universities in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aligarh" class="mw-redirect" title="Aligarh">Aligarh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad (India)">Hyderabad</a>, Urdu is spoken and learnt, and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Urdu" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Urdu">Saaf Urdu</a> is treated with just as much respect as <a href="/wiki/Shuddha_Hindi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shuddha Hindi">Shuddha Hindi</a>.</p>\n<p>Urdu is also the national language of Pakistan, where it shares <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> status with <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_English" title="Pakistani English">English</a>. Although English is spoken by many, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> is the native language of the majority of the population, Urdu is the <i>lingua franca</i>.</p>\n<p><i>Hindustani</i> was the official language of the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="British Indian Empire">British Indian Empire</a> and was synonymous with both Hindi and Urdu.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.co.uk_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.co.uk-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cambridge-Hindustani_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cambridge-Hindustani-37">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> After India\'s independence in 1947, the Sub-Committee on Fundamental Rights recommended that the official language of India be Hindustani:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>"Hindustani, written either in Devanagari or the Perso-Arabic script at the option of the citizen, shall, as the national language, be the first official language of the Union."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>However, this recommendation was not adopted by the Constituent Assembly.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindustani_outside_South_Asia">Hindustani outside South Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hindustani outside South Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Besides being the <i>lingua franca</i> of North India and Pakistan in South Asia, Hindustani is also spoken among the Hindustani diaspora and their descendants around the world, including in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> (in Canada for example, Urdu is one of the fastest growing languages<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>), and in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.</p>\n<p>Hindustani was also one of the languages that was spoken widely in <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a> during British rule. Many older <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burmese</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Indians" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Indians">Anglo-Indians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Burmese" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Burmese">Anglo-Burmese</a> of the country, still know it, although it has had no official status in the country since military rule.</p>\n<p>Hindustani is also spoken in the countries of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>, where migrant labour workers from various countries live and work for several years.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_phonology" title="Hindustani phonology">Hindustani phonology</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grammar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_grammar" title="Hindustani grammar">Hindustani grammar</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_etymology" title="Hindustani etymology">Hindustani etymology</a></div>\n<p>Hindustani contains around 5,500 words of Persian and Arabic origin.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Writing system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hindi-Urdu_orthography" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi-Urdu orthography">Hindi-Urdu orthography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi_Braille" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi Braille">Hindi Braille</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_Braille" title="Urdu Braille">Urdu Braille</a></div>\n<p>Historically, Hindustani was written in the <a href="/wiki/Kaithi" title="Kaithi">Kaithi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_alphabet" title="Urdu alphabet">Urdu alphabets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgregor_912_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgregor_912-28">[26]</a></sup> Kaithi and Devanagari are two of the <a href="/wiki/Brahmic_scripts" title="Brahmic scripts">Brahmic scripts</a> native to India, whereas Urdu is a derivation of the <a href="/wiki/Perso-Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perso-Arabic">Perso-Arabic</a> script <a href="/wiki/Nastaliq_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Nastaliq script">Nastaliq</a> which is preferred calligraphic style for <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>.</p>\n<p>Today, Hindustani continues to be written in the Urdu alphabet, and this is nearly exclusive in Pakistan. In India, the Hindi register is officially written in <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a> (a relative of Kaithi), and Urdu in <a href="/wiki/Perso-Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perso-Arabic">Perso-Arabic</a> script <a href="/wiki/Nastaliq_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Nastaliq script">Nastaliq</a>, to the extent that these standards are partly defined by their script.</p>\n<p>However, in popular publications in India, Urdu is also written in Devanagari script, with slight variations to establish a Devanagari Urdu alphabet alongside the Devanagari Hindi alphabet.</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>Devanagari</caption>\n<tr>\n<th><span lang="hi" xml:lang="hi">\xe0\xa4\x85</span></th>\n<th><span lang="hi" \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';">\xdb\x92</span>\xe2\x80\x8e</span></td>\n<td><i>ba\xe1\xb9\x9b\xc4\xab ye</i></td>\n<td>ai or e</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90</a>/</span>, or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">e\xcb\x90</a>/</span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Because of <a href="/wiki/Indian_English" title="Indian English">anglicisation</a> in South Asia and the international use of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>, Hindustani is occasionally written in the Latin script. This adaptation is called <a href="/wiki/Roman_Urdu" title="Roman Urdu">Roman Urdu</a> or Romanised Hindi, depending upon the register used. Because the Bollywood film industry is a major proponent of the Latin script, the use of Latin script to write in Hindi and Urdu is growing amongst younger Internet users.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Since Urdu and Hindi are <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">mutually intelligible</a> when spoken, Romanised Hindi and Roman Urdu (unlike Devanagari Hindi and Urdu in the Urdu alphabet) are mutually intelligible as well.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sample text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Following is a sample text, Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, in the two official registers of Hindustani, Hindi and Urdu. Because this is a formal legal text, differences in formal vocabulary are maximised.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_Hindi">Formal Hindi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span adhik\xc4\x81ro\xe1\xb9\x87 ke vishay me\xe1\xb9\x87 janm\'j\xc4\x81t svatantrat\xc4\x81 pr\xc4\x81pt hai\xe1\xb9\x87. Unhe\xe1\xb9\x87 buddhi aur antar\xc4\x81tm\xc4\x81 k\xc4\xab den pr\xc4\x81pt hai aur paraspar unhe\xe1\xb9\x87 bh\xc4\x81\xc4\xabch\xc4\x81re ke bh\xc4\x81v se bart\xc4\x81v karn\xc4\x81 ch\xc4\x81hiye.</dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Transcription (<a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a>):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc9\x99n\xca\x8at\xca\x83\xca\xb0\xcb\x90ed\xcc\xaa ek s\xc9\x99b\xca\xb1i m\xc9\x99n\xca\x8a\xca\x82j\xc3\xb5 ko \xc9\xa1\xc9\x94\xc9\xbe\xc9\x99\xca\x8b \xc9\x94r \xc9\x99d\xcc\xaa\xca\xb1\xc9\xaaka\xc9\xbe\xc3\xb5 ke vi\xca\x82aj m\xe1\xba\xbd d\xca\x92\xc9\x99nmd\xca\x92at\xcc\xaa s\xca\x8b\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa\xc9\x99nt\xcc\xaa\xc9\xbe\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaaa p\xc9\xbeapt\xcc\xaa h\xc9\x9b\xcc\x83 \xca\x8an\xca\xb1\xe1\xba\xbd b\xca\x8ad\xcc\xaa\xca\xb1\xcb\x90\xc9\xaa \xc9\x94\xc9\xbe \xc9\x99nt\xcc\xaa\xc9\x99\xc9\xbeat\xcc\xaama ki\xcb\x90 d\xcc\xaaen p\xc9\xbeapt\xcc\xaa h\xc9\x9b \xc9\x94\xc9\xbe p\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe\xc9\x99sp\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe \xca\x8an\xca\xb1\xe1\xba\xbd b\xca\xb1ait\xca\x83a\xc9\xbee ke\xcb\x90 b\xca\xb1a\xca\x8b se b\xc9\x99\xc9\xbet\xcc\xaaa\xca\x8b k\xc9\x99\xc9\xbena t\xca\x83ah\xc9\xaae</span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Gloss (word-to-word):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>Article 1\xe2\x80\x94<i>All</i> human-beings to dignity and rights\' matter in from-birth freedom acquired is. Them to reason and conscience\'s endowment acquired is and always them to brotherhood\'s spirit with behaviour to do should.</dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Translation (grammatical):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>Article 1\xe2\x80\x94All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.</dd>\n</dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_Urdu">Formal Urdu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Formal Urdu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div align="right">\n<p><span lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';">:\xd8\xaf\xd9\x81\xd8\xb9\xdb\x81 1: \xd8\xaa\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa2\xd8\xb2\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd9\x88\xd9\x82 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xb2\xd8\xaa \xda\xa9\xdb\x92 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xb3\xdb\x92 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb1 \xd9\xbe\xdb\x8c\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7 \xdb\x81\xd9\x88\xd8\xa6\xdb\x92 \xdb\x81\xdb\x8c\xda\xba\xdb\x94 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xdb\x81\xdb\x8c\xda\xba \xd8\xb6\xd9\x85\xdb\x8c\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x82\xd9\x84 \xd9\x88\xd8\xaf\xdb\x8c\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaa \xdb\x81\xd9\x88\xd8\xa6\xdb\x8c \xdb\x81\xdb\x8c\xda\xba\xdb\x94 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd8\xa6\xdb\x92 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xdb\x81\xdb\x8c\xda\xba \xd8\xa7\xdb\x8c\xda\xa9 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb1\xdb\x92 \xda\xa9\xdb\x92 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa\xda\xbe \xd8\xa8\xda\xbe\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa6\xdb\x8c \xda\x86\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xdb\x92 \xda\xa9\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd9\x88\xda\xa9 \xda\xa9\xd8\xb1\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7 \xda\x86\xd8\xa7\xdb\x81\xd8\xa6\xdb\x92\xdb\x94</span>\xe2\x80\x8e</span></p>\n</div>\n<p>Devanagari transcription:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span lang="hi" xml:lang="hi">\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa4\xab\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa4\xbe</span> \xe0\xa5\xa7: <span lang="hi" xml:lang="hi">\xe0\xa4\xa4\xe0\xa4\xae\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xae \xe0\xa4\x87\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xa8 \xe0\xa4\x86\xe0\xa4\x9c\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xa6 \xe0\xa4\x94\xe0\xa4\xb0 \xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x81\xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa5\x82\xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa4\xbc \xe0\xa4\x93 \xe0\xa4\x87\xe0\xa4\x9c\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\x9c\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa4\xa4 \xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa5\x87 \xe0\xa4\x90\xe0\xa4\xa4\xe0\xa4\xac\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xb0 \xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa5\x87 \xe0\xa4\xac\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xac\xe0\xa4\xb0 \xe0\xa4\xaa\xe0\xa5\x88\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa4\xbe \xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x81\xe0\xa4\x8f \xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x88\xe0\xa4\x82\xe0\xa5\xa4 \xe0\xa4\x87\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x87\xe0\xa4\x82 \xe0\xa4\x9c\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa4\xae\xe0\xa5\x80\xe0\xa4\xb0 \xe0\xa4\x94\xe0\xa4\xb0 \xe0\xa4\x85\xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa4\xbc\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xb2 \xe0\xa4\xb5\xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa5\x80\xe0\xa4\xaf\xe0\xa4\xa4 \xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x81\xe0\xa4\x88 \xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x88\xe0\xa4\x82\xe0\xa5\xa4 \xe0\xa4\x87\xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa4\xb2\xe0\xa4\xbf\xe0\xa4\x8f \xe0\xa4\x87\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa5\x8d\xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x87\xe0\xa4\x82 \xe0\xa4\x8f\xe0\xa4\x95 \xe0\xa4\xa6\xe0\xa5\x82\xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa5\x87 \xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa5\x87 \xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xa5 \xe0\xa4\xad\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\x88 \xe0\xa4\x9a\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa5\x87 \xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa4\xbe \xe0\xa4\xb8\xe0\xa5\x81\xe0\xa4\xb2\xe0\xa5\x82\xe0\xa4\x95 \xe0\xa4\x95\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa4\xa8\xe0\xa4\xbe \xe0\xa4\x9a\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xb9\xe0\xa5\x80\xe0\xa4\x8f\xe0\xa5\xa4</span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Transliteration (ALA-LC):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>Daf\xca\xbbah 1: Tam\xc4\x81m ins\xc4\x81n \xc4\x81z\xc4\x81d aur \xe1\xb8\xa5uq\xc5\xabq o \xca\xbbizzat ke i\xca\xbbtib\xc4\x81r se bar\xc4\x81bar paid\xc4\x81 hu\xe2\x80\x99e hai\xe1\xb9\x87. Unhe\xe1\xb9\x87 zam\xc4\xabr aur \xca\xbbaql wad\xc4\xab\xca\xbbat hu\xe2\x80\x99\xc4\xab he. Isli\xe2\x80\x99e unhe\xe1\xb9\x87 ek d\xc5\xabsre ke s\xc4\x81th bh\xc4\x81\xe2\x80\x99\xc4\xab ch\xc4\x81re k\xc4\x81 sul\xc5\xabk karn\xc4\x81 ch\xc4\x81hi\xe2\x80\x99e.</dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Transcription (<a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a>):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">d\xcc\xaa\xc9\x99fa ek t\xcc\xaa\xc9\x99mam \xc9\xaansan azad\xcc\xaa \xc9\x94\xc9\xbe h\xca\x8aquq o iz\xcb\x90\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa ke \xc9\x9bt\xcc\xaa\xc9\x99ba\xc9\xbe se b\xc9\x99\xc9\xbeab\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe p\xc9\x9bd\xcc\xaaa h\xca\x8ae h\xc9\x9b\xcc\x83 \xca\x8an\xca\xb1\xe1\xba\xbd z\xc9\x99mi\xc9\xbe \xc9\x94\xc9\xbe \xc9\x99ql \xca\x8b\xc9\x99di\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa h\xca\x8ai h\xc9\x9b\xcc\x83 \xc9\xaasl\xc9\xaae \xca\x8an\xca\xb1\xe1\xba\xbd ek d\xcc\xaaus\xc9\xbee ke sat\xcc\xaa\xca\xb0 b\xca\xb1ai t\xca\x83a\xc9\xbee ka s\xca\x8aluk k\xc9\x99\xc9\xbena t\xca\x83ah\xc9\xaae</span></dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Gloss (word-to-word):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>Article 1: All humans free[,] and rights and dignity\'s consideration from equal born are. To them conscience and intellect endowed is. Therefore, they one another\'s with brotherhood\'s treatment do must.</dd>\n</dl>\n<p>Translation (grammatical):</p>\n<dl>\n<dd>Article 1\xe2\x80\x94All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience. Therefore, they should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.</dd>\n</dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindustani_and_Bollywood">Hindustani and Bollywood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hindustani and Bollywood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The predominant Indian film industry <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> uses dialects of <a href="/wiki/Khariboli_dialect" title="Khariboli dialect">Khariboli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Awadhi_language" title="Awadhi language">Awadhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajasthani_language" title="Rajasthani language">Rajasthani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">Bhojpuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braj_Bhasha" title="Braj Bhasha">Braj Bhasha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bambaiya_Hindi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bambaiya Hindi">Bambaiya Hindi</a>, along with the language of <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> and with the liberal use of <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> for the dialogue and soundtrack lyrics.</p>\n<p>Movie titles are often screened in three scripts: Latin, Devanagari and occasionally Perso-Arabic. The use of Urdu or Hindi in films depends on the film\'s context: historical films set in the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> are almost entirely in Urdu, whereas films based on <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a> make heavy use of Hindi with Sanskrit vocabulary.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urdu_films_and_Lollywood">Urdu films and Lollywood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Urdu films and Lollywood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Pakistani film industry, centred historically in <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, has seen a rise in Punjabi movies lately. Urdu languages have seen a surge throughout Pakistan specifically Karachi, with new age films, and to a lesser extent in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> and Lahore.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustani_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
